<Author>Tomochan
<Content>Great location and staff, not so great rooms I stayed at room 307 for four nights early December. It was a twin with a view of the lovely church! The location can't be beat. It's 10 minutes to Notre Dame, 5 minutes to the Pantheon and about 25 min. walk to the Louvre. I really loved the Charcuterie St. Germaine and the Fromager right as you come out of the Maubert metro station. Eric Kayser boulanger was awesome for breakfast and treats for afternoon snack. The front desk staff members were always friendly, polite and professional. I really love everything about this place except for the beds. The twin beds were smallest I've ever seen. The width of the bed was the same width as my pillow. If I was any taller, I think my feet would be hanging out. I didn't have any issues with the bathroom, the heater or any other facilities. Unless you sleep like you're in a coffin, avoid booking the twin. We booked a shuttle for 17 Euro each to go to CDG. It took about 45 minutes to get there, but we also picked up several passengers along the way.

<Author>drJennyB
<Content>Charming little neighbourhood We really enjoyed staying at this hotel, which is situated in a lovely part of the Latin Quarter. Only a short walk from the Notre Dame, this area is full of lovely bakeries, creperies and little boutiques. We ate breakfast at the Eric Kayser bakery each morning. The staff at the hotel were lovely. They allowed us to check in two hours early so that we could sleep after our long flight from NYC. The room was small but had modern fittings throughout. We were situated on the 1st floor overlooking the courtyard - great because we could walk the stairs to our room but not so great for the noise we could hear from upstairs rooms (like when someone had a bath at 2:30am!). We got a good deal on this hotel by booking directly through the hotel website. Would definitely stay again!

<Author>SHE53
<Content>Great Location, Very Helpful Staff This was our third time to Paris and the Agora Saint Germain was a wonderful choice in the Latin Quarter. Kayer bakery is just around the corner as is Victor Cafe for great beef bourgione. The location is just off St. Germain within easy walking distance to the Notre Dame cathedral. On the weekend there is a wonderful open air market within two blocks. Very easy metro stop as well.The staff was most helpful with restaurant reservations, Moulin Rouge reservations and a shuttle to the airport on the day of our departure.There is a cathedral one block away and the bells do chime on the hour. This can be a little bothersome, but not a real problem.The elevator is small but very wonderful as some Paris hotels do not have elevators.I reviewed this hotel before booking and the reviews were all very right on and most helpful. I would definately recommend this hotel.

<Author>SundayRiver2u
<Content>A Tough Time at the Agora I spend a lot of time in Paris so I'm used to small rooms, but the one at the Agora was not only small, but hot and too noisy to open the window, which overlooked a dark, dank courtyard. The walls were painfully thin and noise from other rooms echoed in the courtyard, so I could hear a neighbor coughing, burping, and allowing other random bodily functions to reveberate throughout the silo of the courtyard. The bedspread was stained, the carpet was stained, the towels were old, rough and scarce - no wash clothes. There also was no safety chain or bolt on the door, and the key confounded me on every occasion. Just a pain to deal with. Internet was extremely expensive so I didn't use it. I loved the staff, they were absolutely wonderful, the location was great, the breakfast was tasty, but I was thankful to be leaving after 2 nights and I really can't recommend this hotel to anyone. I'm disappointed about this because the staff really was terrific and the one saving grace of this hotel.

<Author>citygirl980
<Content>Great place - clean, well located and well maintained The hotel is in a great location on a quiet street just a few blocks from the Pantheon. The rooms were very clean and the beds very firm which for Paris is unusual! The bathrooms were exceptionally clean and very modern. There are a few good bakeries close by, Eric Keyser was my favorite - lines for bread each morning so obviously popular with the locals. There is a local market most days where you can get fresh fruit and vegetables as well as meats and cheeses. Everything that you need is very close by. The rooms facing the interior courtyard/garden are very quiet, highly recommended for people who are noise sensitive. The day staff could speak English, the guys who worked at night were not as helpful but did try their best to accommodate requests.Really good value for the money. I highly recommend this hotel for people who are looking for a clean, well located hotel in the 5th.

<Author>scooterbug
<Content>great location My daughter and I recently spent 3 days in Paris. We had a very pleasant stay at the Agora St. Germain Hotel. First, it appeared from the reviews and what I have been told that hotel rooms in Paris are small. This was my first trip to Paris so I'm not sure how to compare our room with others. The room was neat, clean and nicely decorated although, as I said, on the small side. The room had a desk, television and nightstands. The beds were very comfortable. The bathroom was actually large by comparison, although I think that we had the largest bathroom on the floor. I did reserve the basic room and there are more deluxe rooms available. The front desk was very helpful. It looked like the inside of the hotel had recently been redone and was very pleasant. There was a small but nice sitting area in the foyer. Of note, the church around the corner rings bells at about 8 every morning - however, there is so much to do in Paris we were up anyway! The location was perfect - a 3-minute walk from a metro stop, a 10 minute walk to Notre Dame, many, many excellent restaurants within walking distance and the greatest Bakery (Boulangerie Kayser) around the corner. This hotel is in the Latin Quarter. I had looked at several hotels more in the Saint Germain neighborhood (fancier); however, I'm glad we stayed here - it felt like staying in a small Parisian neighborhood slightly away from all the bustle of Saint Germain but easily within walking distance of everything. Overall, I would recommend this hotel.

<Author>beantown_illini
<Content>Location, location, location The best part of this hotel is the location, right in the heart of the Latin Quarter. Lots of tourist attractions are within walking distance, including the Louvre, Notre Dame, Pantheon, Sorbonne and rue Mouffetard. There are also numerous great restaurants and cafes nearby, and the metro is close, too. All in all, the location really can鈥檛 be beat.Our twin room (#19) was quite tiny, though I suppose the norm by European standards. Still, we weren鈥檛 even able to open the small closet without first moving the nightstand next to one of the beds, which was a bit of a nuisance. The bathroom was clean with a larger than expected bath/shower. The hairdryer looked like some sort of odd vacuum contraption, though, and blew out such little air that it took forever to dry our hair. Recommend packing your own. We never needed to request a wake-up call as there鈥檚 a church at the end of the street and we heard church bells throughout the day and night. It wasn鈥檛 terribly obnoxious, but it quickly became less charming and more annoying.My reviews on the staff are mixed. The woman who is at the desk during the day is very pleasant and helpful. The one time we asked for dinner recommendations, though, she gave us a card for a place around the corner and noted that it was open on Sundays, which it wasn鈥檛 鈥?not a big deal, though. However, the man on duty at night is a lot less friendly and a lot less helpful. Our first night there, we returned after a fairly late night out and were somewhat alarmed to find him sleeping on the bare floor behind the desk! He jumped up, clearly startled, when we came in. Very strange! Also, we requested a cab to the airport very early in the morning the day we checked out and specifically requested ahead of time a cab that would accept a credit card. Asking for this in advance was useless, as the guy at the desk simply went outside and asked the cab driver if he took credit cards after he arrived, which he didn鈥檛. I could鈥檝e done that myself. One other thing that I found bothersome is that the hotel requests that you leave the key with them any time that you leave the hotel. I鈥檝e experienced this before in Europe but it鈥檚 a practise that I鈥檓 not comfortable with, so we didn鈥檛 abide by the 鈥渞ule鈥?and luckily were never asked for ours when we left.Overall our stay was fine and the location was great, but I鈥檇 likely opt for another hotel in the same area instead next time.

<Author>ICVVB
<Content>Quite good hotel - Excellent location The hotel was quite good and the location magnificent.We booked a twin (double) room and stayed 5 nights. We got room 64 which was located on the 6th floor looking at the back alley of the hotel. As a result the room was very quiet (we did not even hear the bells of Saint-Nicolas du Chardonnet church which was located right opposite to the hotel - something that seemed to bother other reviewers in Trip Advisor). The bedroom had double-glazed windows and air-conditioning of a very good quality.The bedroom was relatively small but it was very clean and recently refurbished (note: not so small though by Paris or London standards). The bed mattress was excellent. The bathroom (with shower) was exceptionally clean, good in size and fully equipped.Service was excellent (we got in contact with five different employees at the reception - everyone of them spoke English and were very helpful)The location is magnificent to say the least.Very near there are shops, caf茅s, bistros, brasseries and restaurants etc. Also it is very near or near to Paris' main attractions (Notre Dame, the Louvre, Latin Quarter, Boulevard Saint-Germain, Muse d' Orsay, The Eiffel Tower etc.).There is an excellent boolangerie (bakery) only a few meters from the hotel (it is called Eric Kayser and is located at 8 rue Monge: turn left as you go out of the hotel and a few meters down turn left again and you are in rue Monge). It has excellent croissants and other goodies.Try a stroll through Rue des Ecoles [fist street as you turn right getting out of the hotel] - and try La petite P茅rigourdine on 39, Rue des 茅coles for some excellent and rather cheap French food - beware though the menu is only in French and written on a whiteboard).You can also try some of the numerous establishments found on the nearby Saint-Germain and Saint-Michel boulevards (most of them have English menus).For an excellent dinner at quite good prices you can try Le Petit Prince de Paris it is located at 12, Rue Lanneau (quite near to the hotel - 3 to 4 blocks away and off Rue des Ecoles - better to find it on a map though or at http://maps.google.com/).The metro stop is only two blocks away from the hotel (station Maubert - Mutualit茅 at Boulevard Saint-Germain).Tickets can be used also at buses and RER trains cost:1,60 Euro per ticket, but is a better idea either to buy a carnet of ten tickets at a price of about 11 euros (that is 1.1 per ticket) or even better to buy a Paris-visite card (unlimited travel for 1, 2, 3 or 5 days at 8,50 - 14 - 9 or 27,50 euros per person - see details at: http://www.ratp.info/informer/anglais/paris_visite.phpAll these tickets can be bought at all Metro stations (in every station there are employees where you can buy them - besides vending machines).Try to use the buses if you can (they have an excellent online system of letting you know the itineraries and the waiting time in every bus stop). Buses are quite fast and you can also see a lot of Paris by traveling on them. Otherwise try the Metro.In concluding we had a very comfortable stay, at a good price an in an a more than excellent location.I would strongly recommend this hotel to everyone.

<Author>Loves_to_travel_017
<Content>My 5th time at this great little hotel! I first stayed at Agora St. Germain in 2002 and have stayed 4 times since. It is a block from Maubert-Mutualite Metro stop and easy walking distance to Notre Dame, Jardin du Luxembourg, and many other attractions. The street market is held twice a week right at the Metro and the shops for wine, cheese, meats, fish, fruits and vegetables are all in a line. Between the Metro and Agora is the #1 ranked boulangerie in Paris, Erik Kayser. As you walk from the Metro to the hotel you feel a sense of neighborhood as you join the line at Kayser's for your hot baguette or fruit tarte.The rooms are nicely decorated, comfortable beds and linens, flat-screen TV, and a newly-renovated bathroom -- all can been seen in the hotel website's picture gallery.The interior rooms with windows opening into a small interior courtyard are very, very quiet.For the past 2 1/2 years I have seen the same staff at the hotel and always greeted with a cheerful, Bonjour. Each of the staff was helpful, courteous, and gracious.I highly recommend this hotel and will be back as soon as I can get to Paris again!

<Author>TennesseeTraveler057
<Content>Love the neighborhood We've stayed in the Left Bank several times and by far the Agora St. Germain was the best. We would definitely recommend it to anyone looking for a reasonably priced, comfortable, and friendly place to stay in the Latin Quarter. All of the staff persons were pleasant, helpful, and spoke English. We will likely stay there again the next time we're in Paris. The room was little larger than expected, nicely decorated, comfortable soft bed (we had two twins pushed together), and a good sized bathroom for the price. It's scale and location really make you feel like you're staying in a neighborhood. The Mutualite Maubert Metro is very convenient, as is the market and shops at Maubert, one of the Left Bank's better bakeries (that's saying something) is just around the corner, as are a small grocery and laundromat. Maybe a 8-10 leisurely walk to Notre Dame. Whereas some previous reviews mentioned the church bells, our window overlooked the church and the bells typically did not start until 8 and even then weren't that bad, rather atmospheric actually. Bottom line is if you understand the difference between a small well managed neighborhood hotel and one of the bigger boy chains, and you want the former, choosing the Agora is a good option.

<Content>Great location, small but adquate The hotel is well located, clean and friendly. I'd make a point of asking the hotel for a better room - the tariff in the hotel itself has different rates for various rooms so it is possible that for a few euros more we could have had a better room (had they been available at the time of booking).

<Author>vacances04
<Content>Loved the neighbourhood I booked this hotel based on the comments that I read from Trip Advisor and I was not disappointed. The hotel web site is very representative of the hotel and our room was exactly as the photos and it was kept very clean. Yes, the rooms were very small, but we had every convenience that we could want. We were on the first floor with a nice window looking out onto the church.The neighbourhood was not in the highest tourist area, and you were able to get a feel for the local comings and goings. It was noisy in the daytime with the window open, but we did not spend much time in our room.The church across the street was charming, especially with the church bells waking you each morning! The location was perfect and everything was within walking distance from tourist attractions, local markets, great shopping and fabulous restautants. We did not take the breakfast in the hotel. There was a fabulous bakery just next door (Kayser bakery) and the croissants, pain au chocolat and cheese bread were amazing. The local brasserie (Brasserie Barnum) was serving everything from breakfast to lunch, dinner and the most amazing creme brul茅e. Everywhere we went the service was very friendly. The staff at the Hotel Agoral Saint Germain were very friendly and consistently provided great directions and recommendations for dining. Le Petit Pontpoise was definately a memorable dining experience, not to mention Toustem and Le Buisson Ardent. Coming from Montreal, we had high expectations and were not disappointed. Expensive mind you but worth every morsel. It was a most enjoyable sejour in Paris and I would definately stay at Hotel Agora Sainmt Germain again!

<Author>Laura-GoingPlaces
<Content>Absolutely Fantastic Stayed at this hotel for a weekend break with my boyfriend. I decided on on this hotel because of the location and reviews.What can I say, it was perfect! Rue des Bernardins (the street on which the hotel is situated) takes you straight down to the Seine and the Notre Dame. We used the Batobus to navigate the city and there is a stop at the Notre Dame which was so convenient. We took the boat to the Champs Elysees and walked to the Eiffel Tower (although you can take the boat directly to the Eiffel Tower if you wish). The St Germain area is great with loads of different cafes, bars and shops within walking distance. We came across Tunisian, Japanese, Greek, Indian, Thai, Chinese, Vietnamese, Turkish and of course French cuisine all in the vicinity. There are also designer clothes shops close by for those who can afford it (window shopping only for me!).Our room at the hotel was very modern, clean and comfortable. The minibar is reasonably priced (for a minibar in Paris) and contains a range of soft drinks. I don't know if our room was well sound proofed or the guests were quiet because we didn't hear a peep the whole time. There are TVs in the room with a small range of European channels and CNN and BBCWorld for the English speaking, not that a TV is needed whatsoever as we really only used the room to sleep.We had breakfast at the hotel once and it was fine, a normal continental breakfast as you would expect. We tended to visit the many patisseries, boulangeries and delis in the area!The staff at the hotel were very friendly and helpful. People said before we went that we would find french people rude, but this is rubbish. Even though we spoke little of their language we found that everyone appeared kind and patient (bar 1 moody woman who worked at the metro station in Marne la Valee).I would highly recommend this hotel to anyone, I couldn't fault it in anyway.Paris is definately one of the most beautiful cities I have ever seen and I will go back one day.  
<Date>May 18, 2008

<Content>Mixed feelings about the agora If we had not stayed with friends in this hotel - one of which lived in Paris for 18 months and told us that it is an above average hotel in Paris then I would probably rate this hotel at average. The room is small to say the least. It was hard to get 2 people and 2 suit cases in this tiny little room.The recent reviews on the church bell in the morning are also accurate however it only rang on 3 of the 5 mornings we were there so we must have been lucky because the mornings it did ring we were awake from 6am.As far as the facilities of the hotel - The room is so small that you an not get an ironing board in your room - You have to go to the laundry in the basement to iron your clothes which is a little odd and inconvenient.The bathroom is small but clean.The LOCATION is great - very close to 3 or 4 Metro stations, 5 mins walk from the Latin Quarter and Notre Dame. Cheese shops, Laundromat, wineshopes, supermarkets and Bakeries all very near by.In summary - if this room was any where but Paris I think you would pay a maximum of 75 Euros for the room and that would be fair, but Paris is an expensive city and if you want to stay there and not have to pay over 200 Euros a night, you have to make comprimises - I think you could do a lot worse than the Agora but go with realistic expectations and you will not be dissappointed

<Author>linkSuffolk
<Content>pleasant stay at the Agora Just come back from a three night stay at the Agora St Germain. The hotel is in a pleasant location and only a short walk from the metro. The hotel itself is clean and well kept and we had no complaints about the standard of the rooms. The beds were comfortable but you could tell they were well slept in, clean linen but the bedspeads looked a little tired. Generally the furnishings were fine however. One thing I would recommend is to make sure that you do not get a room overlooking the rather dingy courtyard as there is no view at all and the rooms are very dark. My daughter and I had a room on the outside on the 6th floor and the view was nice and typical of Paris. We went round the corner to a small bar and had delicious coffee and croissants for half the price of the hotel breakfast.

<Author>Fresiandaniels
<Content>A great experience for insomniacs! This hotel always seems to get great reviews. It is both value for money and benefits from wonderfully helpful staff. It is off a main road, so slightly protected from Parisienne traffic noises although it is close to a popular church which gives you no peace whatsoever with loud bell ringing sessions.The rooms are pretty small but refurbished and whilst the bedrooms are pretty middle of the road, the bathrooms have been given a pleasant modern twist.However, beware being allocated a room at the rear of the hotel. These look out on the blank wall of an internal well shaft, so absolutely no views and the rooms are dark as a result. Noise tends to travel up the well. You are shielded from the city noises of the front facing rooms though. All rooms have a problem of paper-thin walls, so if you don't mind hearing your neighbours ' baby crying all night or early morning drinking sessions as friends catch up on their days out - this is for you.It is a great area for food - brilliant boulangeries/cheese shops, restaurants and cafes and it is literally 5 minutes from Notre Dame and the Panthenon.All in all a good experience if you are not looking for pampering or a night's sleep!

<Author>Meg37
<Content>Great location We stayed here for 3 nights the week after Easter, having read the reviews on this site. It was a lovely little hotel, and somehow very familar after all that I had read! The corridors were still being refurbished but the room itself was great - very clean and comfortable, and a lovely bathroom. We had a room on the front of the hotel that had french windows and a small balcony. The church bells at 7.40 in the morning are quite a shock but it all added to the charm! Great location - five minutes to Notre-Dame. The Ile St Louis is a lovely little area with very charming little streets and cafes. We didn't bother with the hotel breakfast - there are several boulangeries around that do a great pain au chocolat! Would also recommend a stroll down the Rue Mouffetard on a market morning and a stop in the Jardin de Luxembourg.Would definitely recommend this hotel in terms of comfort and friendliness - one minor niggle was that the walls seemed to be very thin and we could hear our neighbours quite clearly, but that is more the nature of Parisian buildings than a fault of the hotel's!

<Content>Great hotel in a fantastic location Stayed at this hotel as part of a mid-week break to Paris. I used Tripadvisor to pick a Hotel and travelled on the Eurostar. Make the effort to speak some French and you will be well rewarded! Lots of places to eat and drink nearby.

<Author>bb1976
<Content>Small but perfectly formed We picked this hotel cos it got such a high rating on tripadvisor and are glad we did. The room was very good and the hotel was in an excellent location. Our room was small but had enough storage space that it didn't seem cramped, was very chic and completely spotless. I've stayed in higher star-rated hotels that have had worse rooms. Our room overlooked the courtyard, so didn't have much light, but also no traffic or church bells noise. That said, we could hear quite a lot of noises from the rest of the hotel. The hotel is also undergoing refurbishment, so the corridors were 'works in progress'. The bed was very comfortable and we had the smallest bath in the world in our room, but at least it was a bath! Staff were very helpful. The location really made the Agora, it was within seconds of the metro and minutes of the Seine and Notre Dame (and the RER). What's more, all the little cafes and restaurants locally were great for breakfast or a nightcap. The Latin Quarter was our favourite arrondisement and seemed slightly cheaper than the rest of paris. The Metro is excellent and so fast and the RER is even faster, if a little less attractive. You're not really in Paris to stay in a hotel room, but if you choose the Agora, you won't be disappointed.

<Author>Gerry_Ryan
<Content>Fantastic hotel in a great location Just back from a 3 night stay in Paris and a 3 night stay in the Agora Saint Germain. Unless you go luxury, nearly all hotel rooms in Paris are tiny, however this is an exception. While not huge, the rooms did afford a little walking space between the bed and the wall. Bathroom was small, but again, a little bigger than most hotels I've stayed with in Paris. But the main reason you should chose this hotel is location. It is in the Latin Quarter about a 5 minute walk from Notre Dame. Back behind the hotel (another 5 minute walk away) are all the bars and restaurants that make up The Latin Quarter. We ate here a few times and most of the restaurants are pretty reasonable and serve good food. There is a great vibe around this area, which is full of students having a few drinks. The hotel was being renovated when we were there, mainly aesthetics, paint work etc., but there was no noise at all at night or early morning. We had breakfast on one morning and it was fine, pain au chocolate and croissants. One person did ask for the bacon and eggs (that was advertised), but was met with a very curt, c'est fini. The only complaint I would have about this hotel is that there are no hooks on the back of the bathroom door to hang your towel and if that's all there is to complain about, then it must be good.If you are flying into Paris and staying here, take the train from CDG to St. Michel Notre Dame, then look for the Orange coloured line 10 (about a 2 minute walk), which will bring you to Cluny La Sarbonne and from there, it's just one stop up to Maubert Mutualite. Hotel is about a 2 minute walk from the Metro (it's easier to ask when you get there, rather than me trying to explain it).If I was going back to Paris, I would definitely stay here again.

<Author>TNEG
<Content>Nice little hotel Just back from a week in Paris, where we stayed at the Hotel Agora. We were, overall, quite pleased with the hotel. All of the staff at the reception were friendly and helpful, and spoke perfect English. Our room, on the fourth floor, was definitely not large, but was sufficient for what we needed (a place to sleep after long days of sightseeing!). Everything seemed clean, the beds were comfortable enough, and there was some storage space for clothes. The bathrooms had been recently renovated, which was nice, and were a good size, although it was a little bit of a challenge to avoid getting water from the shower on the bathroom floor! Unlike a previous review, my difficulty with the shower was that the temperature was hotter than I like, so they may have modified that.The location is excellent - about two blocks from a metro station, and 5 minutes from the back of Notre Dame. Also in the immediate area are several cafes, and stores selling cheese, wine, baked goods, meat, etc. We took advantage of this several times, having a picnic dinner one night, and buying baked goods several evenings to eat for breakfast the next morning. We never had the hotel-provided breakfast, which at 11 euros didn't seem like enough of a deal to try with so many other, cheaper, options. For dinner, we found a couple of little streets within 5 minutes walk of the hotel, which had very good restaurants at decent rates.We had just a couple of minor negatives. One was the church across the road - we had read on TA that the bells ring early, but thought that since we were there in winter, and would have the windows closed, they wouldn't be a problem. Don't think this - the bells go off (with a nice little melody) at 7:40 AM 6 days a week. They will then go off on the hour and half-hour. Just be aware of this; it is definitely not the worst thing in the world, but if you are hoping to sleep late in the morning, they will make it more difficult. Also, the rooms are not perfectly soundproofed - one night, we had a group of teenagers in the hotel, and we could definitely notice the noise through the walls.Overall, this is a nice little hotel. It's nothing fancy, so if you are looking for an exceptional experience don't choose it, but if you are hoping for somewhere relatively inexpensive in a good location, this is a good option.  
<Date>Feb 7, 2008

<Author>suefrombrooklyn
<Content>Great little hotel Just returned from Agora Saint Germain. It is a lovely little hotel in a fantastic location. The rooms and lobby are very clean. I stayed for 4 nights. On my first night, I had a room on the first floor that faced a courtyard. There was no light. I asked to be moved and the next day, a room on the 4th floor with a picturesque view of a church was made available. The room was a bit smaller (hard to imagine since all the rooms are small), but the light and air made all the difference. Waking up to a view outside your window really makes the trip special, notwithstanding the church bells ringing every hour or so.The breakfast does not come with the room. I didn't know that until after the fact. At 11 euros, it is not cheap. There are croissants, bread, cheese, yoghurt, hard-boiled eggs, cereal, juice, coffee. Everything was very good and very fresh. If you don't want to think about breakfast, and money is not an issue, the breakfast is the way to go. Around the corner and in the neighborhood are plenty of places to go for breakfast if you want to venture out.The hotel recommended several good places nearby to dine for dinner. I especially liked the husband/wife team at La Maree Verte. They don't speak English, but, are lovely hosts. The hotel is undergoing renovation. The hallways are being painted and are a mess. Each weekday morning, plastic is laid down on the carpeted floors and each evening, the plastic is lifted and the floors vacuumed. Even still, there is plaster dust in the halls. The renovations did not interfere with my use of the room. When in Paris, who spends time in their room? If you are someone who hangs around the hotel during the day, you may want to wait a few weeks (until the end of January 2008) to stay in the hotel. Otherwise, I whole-heartedly recommend the hotel to anyone looking for a quaint small hotel in a great neighborhood.  
<Date>Jan 22, 2008

Stayed here from 11/15-11/23/07 during the transportation strike.Good hotel, good location, nice people  good prices.Post any questions you may have for specifics.Note: an American Breakfast in Paris (Roadside Diner) is about a block away in case you get homesick for American coffee (a bottom cup of joe) or tosted bagel with Phili cream cheese. Taxi fare at seven (7) am with NO Traffic to CDG was $60.00 euros (with no tip and he didn't get one either).In general, a good time!

<Author>shellyNjojo
<Content>Great Location.. Great Hotel! My boyfriend and I just arrived from Paris two days ago and we just had to share our great experience with our HOTEL. Agora Saint Germain is located in the heart of restaurants, grocery stores, churches, etc. It's approximately three blocks away from the Notre Dame and the Metro station was right around the corner (though we had difficulty catching the metro since there was a strike going on.) The staff at the hotel were very friendly and attended to our needs at all times. Our room was always clean with fresh towels everyday. Right on the corner of the hotel is a church that rings every hour and I actually enjoyed listening to this. Our room was located right in the front so we had a great view of the church and the street and I loved how both windows opened up and you can just people watch. There is an A/C and a heater in the room and the heater worked great. My boyfriend actually got sick on this trip and the staff assisted us in finding a doctor the very next day. The staff took the time to call the doctor's office for us and book an appointment. 11 EUROS per person is kind of a lot for breakfast but there are great pastry and croissant places right around the corner for breakfast. Overall, we really really enjoyed our stay at this hotel and would definitely stay here again... You really can't beat the location and the friendliness of this hotel. Thank you for making our stay a memorable one!!!

<Author>NewYorkerJournalist
<Content>Clean, comfortable and convenient! I stayed here back in March as a solo female traveler. (30)I lived in Paris years ago as a student, so I'm very familiar w/the city.The hotel is in a great neighborhood, and if you've got your walking shoes on, you're really in a great spot for walking almost everywhere. Between walking and the metro, this is a great location. You're also not in a heavy touristy neighborhood, so that's great too (not noisy). There are good shops, boutiques, the open-air market as many have noted, tabac, cafes, etc. You're also close to the Seine, which is very helpful while navigating the city! After being out late for a few nights, I walked home or took the metro with no problems, this is a safe area for those concerned about that.The lobby is small and modern, and they were finishing renovations while I was there. The hostess also told me that I was the first to sleep on a new bed in my room, so that's great! There's nothing like old uncomfortable beds....ugh...and mine was brand-new and super cozy. Yes the rooms are small, but if you've travelled in Europe, it won't surprise you. This isn't the USA folks, where buildings are just a few years old....they are centuries old, and who cares, if you are staying in Paris and spending all day in your hotel room, you're nuts! Granted if you are spending big bucks, I'd want a big room too, but not at this price range. My room faced the courtyard, so it was very quiet. I used the alarm on the TV, worked brilliantly. And the bathroom? Super modern, clean and worked very well. And yes, a funky small shower, but again, typical in small european hotels. The water pressure was great--that's usually all that I ask for! But yes--small bathroom, but well-lit, functioned beautifully and it's very modern.I did not eat breakfast there (I think 11 Euro? that's definitely overpriced) And you should do what the parisians do....go out early, get some bread or pastries and then go for a cup of coffee at a cafe and watch the world go by. I think this is a good hotel for single travellers, perhaps mom and daughter getaways, and couples. I'd probably want some more space if I had children, and there are a handful of family-friendly hotels in the area, so I probably would choose another over this one for a family getaway. I also wouldn't call this a romantic hotel, but if you want something basic for a honeymoon or a good, simple base for a couples' getaway and you don't want to spend a lot, it would be fine. But I could think of more romantic areas in the city to stay in other than here. I'd probably love the hotel more if it were slightly closer to Saint Germain des Pres/Quartier Latin, but it's still a good location. And it's quiet---it's not in the rowdy, touristy student areas. Again, very convenient to the metro and a great spot to venture out all over the city. I would also highly recommend staying in the Marais or in the 7th. When in doubt, choose a hotel somewhat close to the Seine, (for navigating purposes) or on a main line/stop of the metro. You'll be glad you did. There are beautiful areas a bit further out, like the 18th and 16th, but if you're not that familiar w/the city, and in Paris only briefly, I would recommend saving those areas for another trip.Also, mgmt was fine. They were helpful and courteous from reservation to checkout, and I a got a good rate. I went online andasked for the lowest rate and I got it. When in doubt ASK for the lowest rate! They want your business and you want a good rate.Clean, comfortable and convenient. A solid choice for a hotel and I would stay here again.  
<Date>Oct 8, 2007

<Author>rain7198
<Content>Great hotel, great location. My extended family (10 of us in all) stayed here for 4 nights and it was wonderful. From check in to check out the staff was friendly and helpful (even though between the 10 of us we speak almost no french). The tiny elevator added to the romance of the surroundings, and the lobby was an fine meeting place for us. my wife and I stayed in room 38 and had a great view of the church across the street. Having been warned about the small rooms, we were pleasantly suprised with being able to walk all around the bed, and plenty of room to store our luggage and accumulated shopping bags! The small cafe around the corner serves amazing croissants and cafe, and there are cute shops nearby, including a toy store we bought gifts to bring home for our kids. As noted Notre Dame, the Pantheon are both a few blocks away, and we walked to the Louvre, Orsey, and Pompadou. Not short walks, but lots to see along the way. My wife and I had to catch a 6:50 am plane on our return, meaning leaving the hotel at 4:15am. Our wakeup call came at the correct time, and the taxi was waiting when we got downstairs. This was my first time in Paris, and I will definately be visiting again, and staying at This hotel!

<Author>MonikafromSurrey
<Content>Don't expect miracles I stayed at this hotel for 2 nights with my Mum in early October. I had booked a twin room with breakfast via a travel agent. When we arrived the receptionist surprised us saying that they ran out of twin rooms and could offer us only a double room. We were willing to pay for an upgrade but all rooms had been taken. It wasn't a great start. The room was a shoe box size and smelt heavily of cigarette smoke. Luckily, the house-keeping was quick to react and in the evening when we came back, it was all fresh and pleasant. The best part of our double room was the bathroom. It was clean and modern although petit. The reception staff was always very friendly and happily offered advice on how to use public transport and taxis. Breakfast was also sufficient with a reasonable selection of pastries and bread and rolls. The cheese board was OK. We loved the location and proximity to a Metro station, lots of shops (bakery, grocery shop, cheese shop, etc) and more importantly to the Notre Dame. I'm not sure if Agora St Germain hotel was the best value for money. Well, it was a busy period in Paris due to the Rugby Cup so many hotels were fully booked and other put up the prices. Given the overall experience, I will consider another hotel in the area in the future.

<Author>MomoftwinsMichigan
<Content>Loved the Agora St. Germain This hotel is a find, not only because of the friendly, helpful staff and comfortable accommodations...but the location can't be beat! Just around the corner is an ATM, the most amazing bakery in all of Paris (stop by Eric Kayser for great breads, pastries and desserts...despite his fame, the line moves quickly...try the pistachio brioche and chocolate croissants!), and a quick walk to numerous bistros, cafes, and museums. The room we had was #49 and it was quiet (soundproof, actually) with a comfortable bed and the bathroom was outstanding for anyplace in Europe...The nearby church bells will serenade you but we did not find that to be bothersome...it only added to the charm of this hotel, which is as clean as can be. Will definitely stay here again. The only downside was that the room was small and there was very limited space for unpacking clothing but this certainly was not a showstopper by any means. Try this hotel...you won't be disappointed.

<Author>rainbowdreamer
<Content>Terrific experience My daughter (age 21) and I just returned from an overnight stay in Paris. We were so pleased with the Agora and would highly recommend it. We booked through the hotel website and the price was under $200. We did not eat breakfast at the hotel but instead went to the cafe around the corner and had a lovely breakfast for 5 Euro - tea/coffee/hot chocolate, croissant or bread and butter, orange juice. Our room 67, had 2 twin beds pushed together, a clean bathroom with bath and shower, and a street view. The hotel is on a very quiet street in the Latin Quarter. The church bells do ring throughout the day, but we really couldn't hear them with the window closed. There are many great cafes nearby, as well as an outdoor market. The metro stop is very close. The front desk staff was so friendly and spoke very good English. The elevator is very tiny. This was our first trip to Paris. We traveled on the Eurostar from London. I would definitely want to come back again to this beautiful city and would choose this hotel as well as recommend it.

<Author>AA82
<Content>Great Hotel for Basic Needs I just got back from a 5-night stay at this hotel. I booked it via their own website, which had much better rates than any of the big travel sites. First, I should state that I was looking for a good value hotel, nothing fancy, but with a clean room and in a great location. The Agora definitely satisfied those needs for me. With their internet rate, I was able to get a superior room here for less than it would have cost for a standard room at what I believe to be comparable hotels in the area.So I booked a superior double room for my boyfriend and me, but when we got to the hotel our room (17) was unavailable because of a problem with the air conditioner. No other superior rooms were available so we took a standard room for the night (room 15) until one opened up the next day. They were very nice and apologetic about this, and we were also understanding and just looked at it as a way to save a little bit of money for one night. Room 15 faced inwards to an air shaft- which they decorated at the ground floor to make a sort of cute little garden- and had a double bed, with barely enough room to walk around especially if you have a lot of luggage. The bathroom is very nice but opens up literally right at the bed, so there is really hardly any privacy even with the door closed. The next day we were moved to room 29 (superior), which faced the street outside, had 2 twin beds pushed together (which I wanted, becuase I think you get a little extra bed that way), and was set up more like any hotel room you'd see in the US. The bathroom was separate from the main room area, and there was a desk. Both rooms had a 19 inch or so plasma tv, which was nice. Both also had a mini-fridge/minibar. I'd say for the extra little bit of money (maybe $50 a night), it is definitely worth it to stay in the superior room, because we would not have been comfortable in the standard for five days. There was just not enough space for us. Both rooms were a little stuffy, but we usually left the windows open while we went out for the day, which the maid closed during her cleaning, and then it was fine when we got back. Housekeeping was good and made up the rooms really nice. Hotel is in a great location- even closer to the Maubert Mutualite metro station than I thought from looking at maps. The 10 metro line definitely isnt the most useful one, but it's just one stop or an extra 5-8 minutes walking to a big transfer station. RIght down the street from the hotel is a strip of food stores- cheese store, wine store, butcher, fish store, bakeries.... literally anything you could need. We went to Maison Kaiser a lot for croissants, baguettes and sandwiches. Very good bakery. Most days there was a nice little market that opened up right there as well. Really great to walk through. If you walk straight up Rue des Bernardins you'll end up at the Seine within a few minutes, and the street turns right into a bridge to Ile de la Cite so it is really a great block to be on. We ate dinner every night in the area- 3 great ones in walking distance, Les Bouquinistes, Le Petit Pontoise, and Le Coupe Chou. We also ate a couple nights in a very touristy area off Rue St. Jacques by Notre Dame... both meals were horrible (in one you'd hear the microwave beeping every couple minutes when people's meals were done!). We should have known. But those other 3 restaurants were truly amazing.Overall, I was pleased with this hotel because it met my needs (which were, admittedly, somewhat basic, but I think similar to what most people look for in a Paris hotel). I wouldn't necessarily go there on my honeymoon, but for a trip where you'll barely be in the room it was a nice place to end the day. We liked that it was very close to the center of things but still a little off on a quiet side street (besides the horrible church bells every 30 min in the morning) and we kind of felt like we were going home every night. Get a superior room and you should be pleased with the quality of the rooms.  
<Date>Apr 4, 2007

<Author>Mykynos
<Content>Perfect base for Paris vacation The Agora was a lovely hotel with a clean, albeit small room and new, modern bathroom. We were there in October and didn't need either heating or air conditioning. There were lovely french doors that opened onto a small balcony for when we wanted some fresh air. The room itself, while small, had everything we needed. It was clean and had enough closet space to put away our two suitcases and hang up our clothes. The king sized bed was actually two twins pushed together and made up separately. The TV got BBC and one other English channel which was more than we needed. The bathroom was spotless but small but had a tub/shower and hairdryer. The whole room was regularly cleaned. There was a small in-room fridge which came in handy. The front desk staff was helpful with making restaurant reservations and giving directions. We didn't have breakfast at the hotel and instead opted to go to one of the many cafes in the area for our morning cafe and crossaint. The location is idea with Notre Dame a 5 minute walk away. We walked to most of the sights. The hotel is in the Latin Quarter but not the sleazy, tourist-ridden part of it. There was still an authentic Paris neighborhood feel to the area and we loved it! There is a Metro stop right around the corner but we more often used the RER Metro stop (C line, I think?) a 5 minute walk away which seemed to have better connections/direct stops. Ask for a room tha overlooks the street and the quaint church across the street; however, be aware that the church bell tolls regularly and loudly. But we loved it and can't wait to go back!

<Content>Ideally placed  The Agora St Germain is ideally situated for a weekend break in Paris being only a short stroll away from Notre Dame. This was our third trip to Paris on the trot and we were looking to visit on a reasonably tight budget without going too down market. Although the Hotel and rooms were smaller than previously experienced, they were found to be very clean and comfortable. The hotel staff were all warm and friendly from the reception, maids and restaurant. The locality has everything on the doorstep from cash machines, bars, restaurants, cafes and tourist attractions to suit everyones pocket. If you want 4* plus luxury then the Agora St Germain is not for you. If you want value for money and a clean, friendly well located base then it definitely is.Martin  Caroline BoothWest Yorkshire

<Content>Very clean and well furnished We had a twin bedded room on the 5th floor with a small balcony (Room 57) which overlooked the street. For breakfast Kaysers is good althought a bit expensive.For evening meals if you turn right after you leave the hotel and turn right along the next street there is a variety of restautrants. The hotel is a few minutes walk from the Maubert Mutialite metro station and is convenient for Notre Dame. We did have a bit of difficulty working out where we were when we arrived at the metro station in the dark and the way to the hotel. I suggest you ask the hotel for directions.

<Author>Mossmania
<Content>Solid hotel Spent five nights here with my wife in October. Overall it was fine. Encountered only minor frustrations - for example, the hotel advertised that they run a shuttle for 18 Euros per person to CDG airport but claimed there weren't enough people to justify the shuttle when we asked for it the night before our departure. They called a taxi instead and promised a rate of 40-50 Euros, although the taxi charged us over 60 Euros. C'est la vie, I guess.Stayed in two different rooms - one with balcony, one facing into interior courtyard. Preferred the balcony room. Both rooms had very nice washrooms. The hotel was quiet. Breakfast was nice, but you could probably put the Euros to better use elsewhere. Perfect if you want to be in the lively Latin quarter.

<Author>Suetonius
<Content>A Hidden Gem Although seasoned visitors to France, it was our first time in Paris.Booking the hotel though Eurostar, it was, consequently, pot luck. . . . but we needn't have worried.The hotel was spotlessly clean and - not knowing the ropes - we had a room ending in 5 (see previous review) . . . . but it was excellent. Admittedly, the room size - while more than adequate - was a tad on the small side, but so what? You don't go to Paris to sit in your hotel room!It had obviously recently been refurbished and was spotless - as for the bathroom, I wouldn't mind one like that myself!The lift was interesting - I almost killed my wife trying to shoehorn both of us and our luggage in - we nearly had hysteria.A typical, small, family run hotel.But the real clincher was the staff.They were friendly, courteous, helpful and spoke far better English than my plume de ma tante French.Situated in a quiet road no more than 100 metres from the Boulevard St Germain, it is superbly placed - especially near the Latin Quarter with its multitudinous bistros  restaurants.I would recommend it to anyone as superb value for money.Unfortunately for our bank account, my wife is already talking about when we go back!

<Author>RonelR
<Content>Good value, great location We have just returned from Paris after a two-week holiday in France. We stayed at the Agora St Germain for three nights and found it reasonably priced, well-positioned, clean and sufficient for our requirements. The room was spacious enough for two people, and the bathroom was attractive and quite big for Paris. We had a room facing the courtyard, which was both private and quiet. The staff were most helpful and very friendly, and both receptionists we dealt with spoke English. The hotel is a hop, skip and jump away from the Blvd St Germain and the Seine, and is also very near Rue Mouffetard, a great area for wining and dining (try Robert's Le Pot a Feu restaurant for great food and great value -- 14.90 euros for a three-course menu!). All in all a very positive experience.

<Author>PrincipalOLG
<Content>What a great hotel! Agora St. Germaine was refered by a relative as a wonderful place to stay and visit Paris. After staying there myself, I felt compelled to write a review. The hotel is very clean and neat, well air conditioned and in a great location. You are a short walk from Notre Dame, the Pantheon, the Louvre, and numerous metro stops. There is excellent food in the Latin Quarter, which is much more fun than the areas that seem geared to tourists. We were even able to find a Starbucks nearby - how lame!There is a bakery just around the corner from the hotel that makes THE BEST CROISSANTS EVER - no contest! You can get an espresso and a croissant for under 2 euro and start your morning off right. That being said, there is no reason to eat the breakfast at the hotel, although they do offer one.Overall, it was a great place to stay. It was far more attractive than any of the hotels near the Eiffel Tower (which cost more) because there is little else in that area except the Eiffel Tower. I would not consider staying anywhere else in Paris.

<Author>sparkggl
<Content>a great 3 star my husband and i stayed at agora st. germain for 6 nights (8/2-8/7) for our honeymoon. i did extensive research before i chose a hotel and i was satisifed with this one and would return again. i was apprehensive at first about this place because my husband stayed at a 5 star and a 4 star in london for the first leg of our honeymoon, and i was afraid that after staying at such nice places i would be disappointed with a 3 star. however, i was pleasantly surprised! yes, the elevator is tiny and the rooms are small, but there are a lot of great points: the bathrooms are really clean and modern, and the bed was sufficient for my husband and i (he's 6 ft. 180 lbs). we had a good view of the street outside our hotel, and my only complaint is that there was construction going on (as there is in a lot of paris) so the noise level was pretty annoying in the mornings. you should call/email them ahead of time to request a room with a view and balcony. we got the view but weren't able to get a room with a balcony. we made our reservations through the hotel website and got an awesome deal.the desk staff was friendly enough but they weren't too helpful with questions about tourist attractions, etc... but then again, they weren't a concierge desk.my husband and i went to a little place to pick up croissants every morning called les delices du forneil (i'm sure i butchered the spelling). they were friendly and their croissants are heavenly. there's a closer place to the hotel called eric kayser that just moved 2 doors down from its previous location and their croissants and pain chocolat look incredible, but they're not so good. but maybe i caught them on bad days. their desserts, however (esp the one with raspberries on top) are amazing. if you get a chance, hit up a gyro stand. they top the gyro with french fries and it's so good. and at 4 euros, it's the cheapest meal you'll ever get in paris.as far as location, the maubert metro stop is really close by. i loved being so close to notre dame and we would often picnic there while gazing at the flying buttresses. the luxembourg gardens are also beautiful for a picnic. i really liked the location of this hotel because it's not too touristy (like the hotels on champs elysee) but it's still close enough to the main attractions. btw, check out saint chapelle. AMAZING.my advice for first-timers: go on the fat bike tour in the evening. it's operated by americans and you get to bike through the city, take a boat ride on the seine, and just have a blast. my husband and i went on the bike tour the day we arrived in paris and i would say that my favorite memory of our trip is riding my bike through the courtyard of the louvre at sunset, seeing the larger-than-life pyramids for the first time with my husband. wow.all in all, the agora st. germain was a great 3 star hotel and we would definitely return.  
<Date>Aug 11, 2006

<Author>NessW
<Content>Good Paris Hotel I think this would be a pretty typical 3 star hotel in Paris but you might find one for the same price that is not as far east as this - The Agora St Germain was about 500m from Notre Damn metro stop, there are 2 others stops closer but Notre Damn is on more lines so we felt like we walked alot to get to and from the hotel from here, the walk along the river is lovely but we were usually exhausted from a full day and just wanted to get off the metro and be home!! I would definately stay on the left bank again but would look for a hotel slightly more central.The rooms are very small but modern - the smallest rooms we encountered on our 4 week trip through Europe. You really wouldn't want to spend much more time in your room than sleeping  changing. The bathrooms although tiny are very modern and clean.The patisserie around the corner is fanastic for breakfast (Eric Kayser). The hotel stored our bags while we went to Loire Valley for 2 nights which was very convenient and it looked like our bags hadn't been touched at all while we were away. Our air conditioning didn't work for 2 nights and it was very very hot, we asked for a discount becuase we had double checked that the hotel had air con' before we confirmed our stay but the manager wasn't on and we have since emailed and they will not offer us any credit - except one free night next time in Paris - we are in NZ which is 24 hours flight from Paris so I dont know when we will be back!! We didn't find the staff overly helpful when we asked questions about tourist attractions but they were friendly enough. We didn't experience any of the French rudeness that we had heard about, we had a phrase book and always tried our best in french and most people would reply in english laughing at us!! Plus the beds are not full sized doubles my husbands feet were over the edge (he is 6foot1) and we were very squashed and are not really big people!!

<Author>LOUISE1HAWTHORN
<Content>c'est manifique!! Have just returned to England from a sweltering Paris absolutley thrilled with the Agora. Very modern, almost boutique style lobby and room and fantastic bathroom ( room 47) Air conditioning was excellent and much appreciated!Couldn't be better situated; one of the best patisseries in Paris around the corner ( Eric Kayser) also try their violet ice cream but maybe not for breakfast!, a little supermarket open selling ice and bottled water, very handy in the 99 degrees! Quickest way to the river is left out of the hotel and straight down Rue Bernadins , about 3 minutes. The lovely cheese shop on the square near to the hotel vacum packs cheese to bring home and 4 lots just about fit into our room refridgerater. On the last day, we couldn't handle dragging our cases through the streets and couldn't get the airport shuttle from the hotel as you have to book in advance. However, we hailed a cab from outside the hotel taking us straight to Charles d Gaulle and it cost only 2 euros more than the shuttle!All in all a fantastic stay, yet again tripadvisor gets it right and I will recommend this hotel to anyone!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Clearn and affordable hotel in a great location! My wife and I stayed at this hotel for 6-nights. We had a room on the 6th floor. Details of our room:- Modern looking room - Double-bed. A little hard but comfortable enough (you'll do enough walking in Paris that you'll sleep fine at night)- Room size was small as expected, but they did a great job utilizing the limited space with shelves, closets, etc.- Rooms were very clean.- A/C was a portable unit, which required a hose to be stuck out the window. This meant the window had to be propped open. I was a little concerned that noise would be an issue, but it wasn't at all.- Bring a electric converter (if from the U.S.). If you forget, you can get one at BHv, like we did.- Small flat screen TV, which has the alarm clock built-inDetails of our stay:- The staff was extremely friendly, but unfortunately were not overly helpful. We had asked about places to eat, where to get the Paris Museum Pass, and which metro stop to get off when going back to the airport. None of those questions could be answered (perhaps we just happened to ask the wrong staff member).- You leave your room key at the desk every time you exit and just ask for it when you come back. Convenient not to have to carry it with you during the day.- We arrived early in Paris, but unfortunately weren't able to check-in until 2pm. Hotel let us store our luggage until check-in, so it was fine.- Yes, the elevator is small, and it took about 2 seconds to get over that fact.Location- Great location! There's a wonderful bakery around the corner if you take a left out of the hotel, then a left at the first street (Rue Monge). The pain-au-chocolat was our favorite! Also, you're in walking distance to Notre Dame, Saint Chapelle, Ile St. Louis (eat ice cream here!), and Hotel de Ville (has shopping nearby). There are also a ton of restaurants and cafes open late on the way to Hotel de Ville. Also, close to the Maubert-Mutualite metro stop.- The brasseries nearby on St. Germain right off of Rue Monge are only so-so. If you want great crepes, you need to continue north on Rue Monge (towards the river), which will turn into Rue LaGrange. There's a wonderful crepe place across the street from the Chinese Restaurant, with a friendly staff (and they speak English).OverallWe would definitely stay here again. The location is great, the staff is friendly, rooms are clean, and the price is affordable. I can definitely see how this is a 3-star hotel, however, I think it ranks above most 3-star hotels.

Nice outdoor market by Maubert Metro on Saturdays.Take a taxi from train station to hotel 18 euros and have the front desk reserve a shuttle back to CDG for 18 euros per person. Would return to property.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A lovely little hotel Hotel Agora St-Germain is a lovely, little three-star hotel in the Latin Quarter. The closest metro is Maubert-Mutualitie. The lobby is vaguely art deco and the room, though small, was comfortable. As is typical in Paris, there are tall windows. Ours faced the street and a typically Parisian street scene: church, flowers, trees, rooftops. Breakfast was a little expensive--10 euros--but fresh and delicious. We had it brought to the room and ate with the windows pushed open and the sun streaming in.The staff, especially a woman named Aline, was very helpful and knowledgeable. Although it's a little far east, it's only a few blocks from Notre Dame and the river. We booked online in advance and felt we had gotten a good deal. I will definitely return.

<Author>ClaudiaB
<Content>Great Location and Helpful Staff My husband and I stayed here for 5 nights earlier this month. The very best thing about the hotel is the location and the second best thing is that the air-conditioning in the rooms works quite well. (Having stayed in European hotels where this is not the case I was very grateful for this - it was very hot when we were in Paris.) I would also be remiss if I did not mention the helpfulness of the front desk staff - especially Aline. She gave us great info about the immediate and went to great effort to help us find whatever we needed! On the down side, the rooms are small and a bit shabby - but quite clean. The elevators are TINY and the hall is narrow. If you anticipate spending much time in your room you might want something larger. The TV was fine - I did not anticipate English-speaking channels and we had fun trying to follow the storyline with our very limited French. We would certainly stay here again.

<Author>skcollins74
<Content>Loved the Agora St. Germain! I stayed at the Agora St. Germain by myself for my first trip to Paris from May 10-16. This hotel was the perfect choice for a good 3 star hotel. Simple but with everything you need. All of the staff were extremely helpful and pleasant, especially Aline. And the location could not be more perfect. It's located on a small street just around the corner from St. Germain Blvd. The Maubert Mutualite Metro stop is just around the corner, as well as a taxi pick-up. It took me probably 3 minutes to walk to Notre Dame (San Francisco fast walk) where you can catch the Batobus. It's a great central location for exploring Paris. I walked just about everywhere or took the Batobus.There is a small market just around the corner 4-5 days a week where you can buy fish, cheese, spices and plenty of jewelry and clothes. The are tons of cafes nearby and it's an easy walk down St. Germain Blvd. for even more.I fell completely in love with Paris and booked another trip for this year just 3 days after I returned home. And I was so pleased with the Agora that I am staying there again. This isn't luxury, but a perfectly comfortable place to lay my head and call home base.

<Author>6boys4me
<Content>Perfect hotel! So glad we chose it!!! We just returned yesterday from a one week stay in Paris to celebrate our 25th anniversary. I had spent 2 weeks reasearching hotel reviews as I wanted something special, but couldn't afford the likes of the Ritz Carlton. And we couldn't have been happier with the Agora! It was super clean, fresh soft sheets, newly remodeled bathroom, (very modern) We got a room (#49) with a view of the beautiful old St. Nicholas du Chardonnet church across the street. The room was sound proofed and very quiet. And we just loved hearing the gentle peal of the church bells in the morning. It was so charming!!! The staff was terrific (especially Elaine) and there's air conditioning in the room to keep you comfortable, along with a flat screen plasma t.v. and built in blow dryer (which was great not to have to bring our own and try to find electrical adapters to use over there.) The elevator is tiny as others stated. But so what! You are always free to take the stairs next to the elevator. That's what we did going down. Taking it when going up to our room, and wasn't a problem to have to stand close to each other for 60 seconds. The hotel lobby was nicely appointed, and comfortable, with a morning paper in English to catch up on world news.  The breakfast room downstairs was very nice, and yeah, 10 euros apiece seemed a bit high for the breakfast, but we did eat there twice in the week, and it was kind of nice having as much coffee as we needed without having to pay 5 euro for one cup elsewhere. There's fresh baked croissants, Pain au chocolate (chocolate croissant), baguette, cheeses, butter, jam, cereal, juice, tea, coffee, yogurt. And the french yogurt is REALLY good. Different than we get in the U.S. Much creamier! So while you can certainly go to a local pastry shop or cafe for breakfast, there's times when it's pretty convenient to just go downstairs and enjoy your fill of coffee, and plan your day out in the peace of the breakfast room, rather than on the busy sidewalk. You've got room to open your metro and city maps on the table.  The location is PERFECT! You've got an ATM machine just outside the hotel, a 5min. walk to Notre Dame Cathedral, 5 min. walk to shops, metro station, farmer's market, restaurants, etc. A note to anyone who's never been to Paris: buy a one week pass for the metro, and at the same window, also buy the one week museum pass. A MUST!!! this way you don't have to wait in the long lines at the Lovre, (over 2 hrs wait otherwise) or Musee d'ORsay, or Palace at Versailles. You can just go to the front gate for reserved tickets. Well worth the money spent. You can get all over the place with the metro, it has good connections. And the pass also allows you to use the trains or buses within a certain region. If you do go outside your area, then you'll just have to pay a couple euros extra to exit the station. No big deal. I'd recommend this Agora St. Germaine to anyone, and wished I hadn't wasted so much time looking at all the other hotels. I'd go back in a heartbeat, if we ever go again!  
<Date>May 22, 2006

<Author>Cunningham8
<Content>Good location This hotel is in a wonderful location as detailed in previous reviews. It is a small hotel with small rooms and bathrooms and an extremely small lift - be warned! However, I have stayed in 3* hotels in Paris on three other occasions and this hotel did not quite match up to the standard of the others.

<Author>cestbon
<Content>cestboncestbon completed a 6 night stay in Paris at the Agora St Germain (March 23-29)and found the hotel met all expectations and then some....getting the nits picked first...the hotel lobby was being renovated and was unusable for anything other than collecting your room key (you had to turn it in when you left)and the hotel stored material in the narrow hall (we had rooms 4  5) this was some remedied by the time we left and the lobby was pleasently comfy for a small group to meet in. The staff was tremendous. Period. They went above the call and helped one of our party confirm airline connections and aquired a taxi during a general strike day....and everybody appeared on cue!..always pleasant and helpful for eating recommendations and help avoiding the protestations...the location is wonderful for jumping off into old Paris being two blocks from Notre Dame and Ile de St. Louis and Blvd St Germain a main street for bus connections and good restaurants. We had a double (5) and a triple (4) that were very comfy though for the same price I would reequest the triple..(double bed and a single). Each room had a small refrigerator and a simple closet for clothes and room for a suitcase under...two simple chairs..a very nicely appointed and apparently newly remodeled bathroom...large by European standards. We had some difficulty regulating the heat in the rooms.(too warm) and we had rooms that looked across an interior courtyard into the lobby....had to make sure the drapes were closed getting dressed... there was no problem with noise that doesn't occur in any hotel. Around the corner was a small neighborhood outdoor market that occurs on tues/thurs/sat that had a little of everything. At the same place was a cheese shop, mini grocery, pharmacy, bakery, and small cafe for your pleasure. ATM's and bank branches are very convenient. I would recommend this hotel and will stay there again.

<Author>rubydc
<Content>Perfect for a single woman I stayed at the Agora in July, after being moved from their sister hotel (I arrived to find I had been moved, so I never stayed at the other). No problem, and they were very polite and courteous about the switch and greeted me by name. I had a single room, which was small but just right for me (I am small!) and it had everything I needed. It was quiet and cozy with a comfy bed. The A/C leaked water, but I really didn't need to use it. I found the room very clean and the area incredibly convenient. I was traveling alone (I am a youngish single woman) and found the staff to be very helpful and they always recognized me as I came and went, which put me at ease. I really enjoyed the breakfast room every day, and by the end of my stay the Agora felt like home. Also, I was there during the London subway bombings and had to extend my stay as I could not travel to London, my next stop, for a couple of days. They were very accommodating, and extending literally at the last minute was no problem at all. Also, my rates were excellent. I have traveled to Paris a number of times, and I will stay at the Agora, no question, on my next visit.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good clean hotel not very responsive with email confirmations My husband and I just returned from stay in Europe (London/Paris). We stayed at this hotal Nov 21-26, 2005. We booked this hotel through American Express Travel, the same as with our London Hotel. Before leaving for our trip, I decided to contact the hotel via email to confirm our room reservations for both hotels. The hotel in London, had a toll free number so I called and confirmed my reservation. The Hotel Agora St. Germain did not so I decided to email the hotel directly. Well, needless to say, I did not receive a reply back before leaving. I was a little concerned but since the hotel in London saw my reservation made through Amex, my husband just said don't worry about it and we went off on our trip. When we arrived at the hotel and en route to the hotel on the chunnel I was thinking about the reservation. Well, guess what.... they didn't have our reservation. Not their fault, in all fairness, it was travelocity whom sold the rooms to Amex... Amex thought everything was confirmed and passed the information to us. So, we felt confident about the choice but we were wrong. The woman at the checkin counter gave us a room anyway but said she wasn't sure if we could stay there the entire trip.... and we would have to take care of it with American Express. Lucky for me I had taken my cell phone and was able to contact American Express. Althought the call cost me .99 cents a minute, it was well worth it since they faxed over the confirmation and called the hotel directly to confirm receipt. This was taken care of within the hour of our arrival. However, starting out like this didn't really leave a good feeling... especially since the lady kept telling us that now she has a problem with people checking in on the 24th Nov. and seemed very frustrated that this happened on her watch. That didn't make things better... to be honest it added to my frustration. My husband had to calm me down of course and reason with me not to lose my temper since it was not really her fault. However, I did email them directly and at a minimum would have expected an reply email with .. we don't have a reservation for you... etc. I mean they did have a PC with internet access at the front desk. My husband did notice there was a fax on the floor. It is very possible that their carelessness could have caused this confusion and inconvenience. As for the room.... we stayed in room 69. The room was facing the street on 6th floor with a little balcony.. too little to step out but could open window/door and peek out. Heard very little noise. The bathroom was very clean when we arrived and the daily maintenance of same was pretty good. The bed was comfortable. They have a desk with a chair and a small ottoman. Heating in the room was fantastic. lighting was proper. The closet could have been in a different location.. Although the closet was big enough for Paris standards, to get to it and access clothing was a bit tight since it was right next to one of the nightstands... The luggage was easily stored under the closet... unless of course you have monster luggage. We like to travel light so our standard carry-ons fit fine. The room had a very delightful and clean aroma after it was cleaned daily. Oh... and great hot water and water pressure.What I didn't like was that they didn't provide you with shampoo soap and conditioner as separate items. They had a dispenser by the sink and in the shower stall with their so-called combination soap/shampoo/conditioner which really stunk if you asked me. We used it as soap since we had brought our own shampoo. No shower cap, no sewing kit, no other perks except for lotion. They have a mini fridge in the room with refreshments and a beer bottle opener and they do have corkscrews at the front desk you can borrow if you buy some wine.The rest of the staff was very friendly and helpful.All in all is what we expected.... small, clean, tastefully decorated room. My husband just fell in love with the bathroom so I'll give them kudos for that. If it wasn't for that reservation snafu and the front desk person's indifference maybe our rating would have been better.Remember, confirm your reservation by phone with hotel directly. Faxes may end up on the floor below one of their counters/furniture. Oh and don't bother with the Breafast... There are plenty places you can buy a coffee and a croisant for under 4 Euros nearby or do as the parisians do... get a crepe to go... Cheers..and buon voyage  
<Date>Nov 27, 2005

<Author>HastingII
<Content>Charmed by the Agora! We just spent a fabulous six-night honeymoon in Paris at the Agora St. Germain Hotel in Paris! Only three blocks from the Maubert-Municipalite Metro and Notre Dame, this charming hotel made the stay perfect. The staff, particularly Eric, was friendly and helpful, the breakfasts were great, and our room was kept clean every day. We had a large (for Paris), modern bathroom and even thin-screen, wall-mounted TV that allowed for more space. There are many Bistros and Brasseries just around the corner that serve excellent meals, and one can stop at one of the several patisseries for sandwiches, breads, and desserts any time of the day--there's even a small grocery nearby. I've been to Paris twice before, both times in Montmartre, but from now on will only stay at the Agora. We even walked to the Eiffel Tower on the first day, as the weather was perfect the entire week. Our tip: take the dinner cruise on the Bateaux Parisienne, and on another night, see the show at the Moulin Rouge. The Lido was only OK. Take the airport shuttle to and from DeGaulle Airport (18 euros)--the RER-to-Metro and hike to the hotel is tiring!!! We booked through Expedia 2 months in advance after reading the reviews in Tripadvisor.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great little spot to stay I was worried about going to a 3 star hotel in Paris, expecting tiny rooms that you wouldn't be able to 'swing a cat in' and possibly a bit grotty. However, I think we had a deluxe room, as it was a decent size, clean and seemed to have a newly renovated en-suite (bath with a shower). While we were there someone had complained about a room (I don't know why), they were moved to another room and got a night free. It is close to a number of Metro stops, the lively eating area of Saint Michael, the farmers market nearby which is amazing and to view the queue to the bakery on a Sunday morning is unique. The staff were friendly and it was a great spot to stay in and we would go back.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A+ Hotel Stay We rate this hotel a 4+: a useful Metro line, two convenience stores, a farmer's market, and two bakeries are within 1-2 blocks. The hotel was pristinely clean and the service friendly and helpful. The church bells across the street are charming, but reconsider staying here if you are a late riser--they ring for Mass at 7: 40 and then every hour after that. The street noise was also a bit loud on some days, but just a smidge noisier than other neighboorhood hotels we've stayed at in Paris. We did not get the 12e breakfast in our package, but would consider this on a future stay as coffee, tea, etc. outside the hotel is routinely 5e; add a crossaint and tip and you may as well have spent the 12e for a full and hearty breakfast. This hotel does include a refrigerator, which really is a plus. Stock up at the 8 Huit around the corner (I recommend the myrtille yogurt). Have a wonderful time in the most beautiful city in the world.
