<Author>PippyThePixie
<Content>Would stay here again Just got back from a week in Paris and was very pleased with this hotel. The room was small with 2 single beds pushed up together but separate bedding. It was clean, towels and bedding changed everyday, and I guess it had been renovated recently. The bathroom had been completely redone and all the fittings seemed brand new. The shower worked very well indeed (just the job after a hard day's sightseeing). There was even an LCD tv on the wall and there was also air con, though it didn't work brilliantly (poss because it was very hot when we stayed there and I think everybody had theirs on full blast too). That's the only criticism really. Breakfast in the basement consisted of croissants, cereal, coffee etc but would also like to mention the patisserie round the corner which turned out more expensive than the hotel breakfast but is well worth at least one visit so you can eat like the Parisiens do. Receptionists were always very helpful, spoke good english, and organised a shuttle for us to CDG for total 36 euros for two of us (not bad considering we had to go at 5am!). But I think it does help if you make the effort to speak a bit of french. Nearest Metro (Maubert Mutualitie) only 5 mins walk away and restaurants? Well take your pick. Recommend the Beouf Bourgignon at Chez Rene on Boulevard St Germain. Unbelievable !!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>updated bathrooms give it superior rate Third time to Paris, first time on the Left Bank. Stayed at the Agora for 7 nights in a 'superior double/twin room'. What makes it a 'superior' room is the newly renovated, modern bathroom. Great shower! The decor is no different than the standard rooms, nor is the size and you don't get 2 chairs. The linens are standard but the carpeting could certainly use a steam clean. Very small twin beds so if you are a tall person, be prepared for your feet to hang out (I'm 5'3). Oh, and the beds are put right together but with separate bedding. The room was very small but standard for Paris - no place to put your luggage so you have to do the two-step around the beds. Only on the top floor do you get an actual balcony and they don't cost any more than lower floors. The rooms are somewhat soundproof, we didn't hear any voices, just the doors closing and the water running from toilets and showers. Although, our neighbour pounded on our door to ask that the TV be turned down - and in all fairness, the tv was probably a little loud because of the air-conditioning which worked great! My 3rd floor room faced the front of the street and was a little noisy at night with students and the neighbourhood teens partying it up. Breakfast is not elaborate and costs $12euros. There is a patiserrie around the corner that is very pleasant and you can sit in or out - it closes for the month of August!The staff is friendly and helpful, not rude and they speak english. For a special rate of $135euros, it really is okay, but if you take the chance of walking in off the street for a room it's something like $90euros at the same hotel! In the summer there is no difficulty finding a room in Paris so take your chance when you get there.The neighbourhood is okay, there is main stream shopping up the street and high end boutiques on St. Germain de Pres. The Luxembourg Gardens are within walking distance as is Notre Dame. I prefer staying on the Right Bank - it's more exciting/pleasant and closer to the main attractions and the food is way better, and the the men are better looking.  
<Date>Aug 21, 2005

<Author>joekg
<Content>Loved the Agora Saint Germain What a great hotel. It is small, not your American big city Hilton, but at its reasonable cost it is perfect for the modest Paris traveler. The location is perfect- we walked from it to Notre Dame in 10 minutes and either walked or took the Metro (station 5 minutes away) anywhere in Paris in 20 minutes or less. And that bakery around the corner......cafe, croissant, and hand squeezed orange juice each morning. Saint Germain is a fun street with lots of cafes, bakeries, cheese stores, and more within a few blocks. The rooms were very modest but comfortable, the bathroom clean and very functional. The front office staff was helpful (though the weekend and evening staff were not quite as familiar with the area). I have no reservations in recommending Agora Saint Germain unless you want to pay more to get more.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Better avoid My friend and I stayed at the Agora St.Germain in June and were quite disappointed. The woman who welcomed us was simply rude and unfriendly, although the rest of the staff was friendlier. Our room was small, with barely enough space to walk around the bed. Furniture was tasteless and not adequate (no single drawer, the closet was very small, only one chair). The bedspread looked like it hadn't been washed for a long while. The hotel has also larger and probably more comfortable rooms, more expensive than our standard double room (still, I don't feel that in a three-star hotel I should move up to the category superior, to get two proper chairs in a double room). The bathroom met the standards of a three-star hotel more than the rest. Still, it was very small (never been in a french three-star bathroom that didn't have a bidet); the door couldn't be locked, showering would produce a flood on the floor, and we experienced at least twice a sudden shortage of warm water, while taking shower. It was clean, but one couldn't call it spotless, as we could spot a variety of other guest' fingerprints on the door handle and towel hangers, and they were still there after one week. The location is of course very good, as other TripAdvisor users pointed out, but there are many other hotels nearby, and if you make your reservation well in advance (which we didn't do), you can have plenty of choice and definitely pick a better option.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great hotel, great location We (a party of 10) stayed at the Agora St. Germain in February. A room was given to us to stow our bags and freshen up (we arrived in the AM, before check in). It's a lovely hotel, the staff is very nice. There is renovation going on (our room smelled very much of paint, but we did get used to it -- our room was post renovation and lovely), but it doesn't start until 9ish and we were already up and out by that time. The breakfast is adequate, fresh croissants and bread, decent coffee (of course one can do better going to a cafe, but no one in our party complained about breakfast at the hotel). As a plus (for European hotels anyway), breakfast is not automatically included in the hotel bill, so there is no check out haggling over whether or not you had breakfast. The elevator was out one evening, which made a long, circular walk upstairs for 2 in our party (they didn't complain much -- it was their first trip to Paris and had carry-on luggage only, but it might be something you want to consider if you're traveling heavier). I would stay here again in a heartbeat!! A GREAT value -- in August I stayed at a hotel near the Louvre for almost double the price per night and the room was only a tiny bit larger and the bathroom was not nearly as nice. The Agora has a very nice location in what I felt was a safe neighborhood. One thing -- while I found the church bells (there is a church across the street) charming, they might wake a light sleeper.  
<Date>Mar 4, 2005

<Author>dupontgrl
<Content>It's great...but maybe not right now! The hotel has a lot of great points: super location, friendly staff, clean  well-kept rooms. Also, if you can get a free breakfast included, it is very filling (baguettes, croissants, cheese, jam  yogurt). The rooms are also a good size for Paris.But, keep in mind that the hotel is currently undergoing a major renovation. Since the hotel is small, the construction is very loud (we're talking hammering and drilling), which starts every morning during the week at 9 AM. It's especially unbearable if it's being done in the room next to you. Also, due to the construction, the elevator was broken during our stay, and sometimes the toilets wouldn't flush right away. Once again, these are all just temporary issues.A couple of extras: if you don't get a free breakfast at the hotel, don't pay for it. While it's filling, you're in Paris, and it's worth shelling out a few Euros for a much better baguette or croissant in the morning. In fact, there's a great boulangerie right around the corner from the hotel.Also, the hotel directions from CDG instruct you to take the RER B train to Cluny Sorbonne. This is very easy, but keep in mind there's no Cluny Sorbonne exit on the RER B train. The train exits at St. Michel/Notre Dame, and there is an underground tunnel that connects you to Cluny Sorbonne. If you do exit at St. Michel, no worries, you're still close enough to the hotel to figure it out.

And the lady who runs the place is extremely pleasant. She will also do eggs if you wish. The location of the hotel is great as other reviewers have pointed out.

<Author>motek1849
<Content>Great location, nice staff, mattresses are soft. Just back from a 4 night stay in early September at the Hotel Agora St. Germaine. This is a fabulous neighborhood, with a great location. Near to a Metro stop, shops, boulangerie, food kiosks, ethnic food restaurants. Several internet cafes nearby. The best part of the hotel was location. <Content>Loved The Hotel, Neighborhood We stayed at the Agora Aug. 13th-Aug. 19th. I absolutely loved this hotel. I will stay there again the next time I visit Paris.
